    [Original] Navigating the complexities of Cell and Gene Therapy supply chains
    Cell and gene therapies (CGTs) represent a transformative advance in treating previously untreatable conditions, but their supply chains are among the most complex in the pharmaceutical industry. These therapies require precise coordination across multiple stagesâ€”cell collection, manufacturing, and final deliveryâ€”each time-sensitive and dependent on strict temperature control, regulatory compliance, and unbroken chain of custody and identity. Challenges include complex logistics, real-time tracking, regulatory adherence across jurisdictions, data integrity, stakeholder coordination, scalability, and risk management. Delays or disruptions can jeopardize therapy viability and patient outcomes. To address these challenges, developers need robust strategies incorporating advanced cold chain logistics, predictive analytics, standardized processes, and strong partnerships. Technology integration for traceability, monitoring, and communication is essential. However, building in-house supply chain expertise is often impractical due to the high cost, specialized knowledge, and infrastructure required. Catalentâ€™s Case Management Services offers end-to-end supply chain coordination tailored to individual CGT programs. The service includes program onboarding with optimized shipment strategies and mock shipments, dedicated case managers for continuous monitoring, scheduling support for collection, manufacturing, and delivery, and strict adherence to chain of custody and regulatory compliance. Catalentâ€™s global network and partnerships with premium courier services enhance reliability and speed. One client faced significant delays due to misclassified Harmonized Tariff Schedule (HTS) codes, customs bottlenecks, and extended transit times. Catalent implemented revised shipment strategies and established direct courier communication, reducing delivery times from 10 days to 52 hours on the USA-Australia route (79% improvement) and from 5 days to 43 hours on the USA-Europe route (64% improvement). These gains ensured timely patient access without compromising oversight. Catalentâ€™s expertise, technology, and patient-centric approach enable developers to focus on innovation while ensuring therapies reach patients safely and on time. With operations across 40 global sites and thousands of scientists, Catalent supports the development and delivery of billions of doses annually. As a leading contract development and manufacturing organization (CDMO), Catalentâ€™s Patient First approach underscores its mission to improve health outcomes worldwide. For more information, visit www.catalent.com.

    [Original] Small and mighty: single-domain antibodies pack a biological punch
    VHH antibodies, also known as nanobodies or single-domain antibodies (sdAbs), are compact, stable, and highly engineerable fragments derived from heavy chain-only antibodies found in Camelidae species. First identified in 1993, their unique structureâ€”comprising a single variable domain (12â€“15 kDa)â€”enables superior tissue penetration, access to hidden epitopes, and the ability to cross biological barriers like the bloodâ€“brain barrier. The FDA-approved therapeutic Caplacizumab (CabliviÂ®) in 2018 marked the first clinical milestone, paving the way for growing interest. By the end of 2025, five VHH-based therapeutics are expected to gain global regulatory approval, with over 49 VHH sequences in clinical development. The global VHH market is projected to grow at a CAGR of approximately 15%, driven by applications in oncology, immunology, and diagnostic imaging. VHHs offer distinct advantages over conventional monoclonal antibodies. Their simple, stable structure ensures robustness under extreme thermal and chemical conditions, enabling use in challenging formulations such as inhalation or oral delivery. Unlike IgG antibodies requiring mammalian expression systems, VHHs can be efficiently produced in microbial systems like *E. coli*, yeast, and plants, reducing manufacturing costs and accelerating timelines. Their lack of a light chain provides exceptional engineering flexibility, allowing modular design for multi-specific formats, fusion with effector domains (e.g., enzymes, toxins, Fc regions), and rapid development of complex therapeutics. Despite these benefits, VHH development faces significant challenges. The absence of established CMC (chemistry, manufacturing, and controls) pathwaysâ€”unlike the decades of GMP experience for IgGsâ€”creates regulatory uncertainty and can extend development timelines. Discovery hurdles include limited sequence diversity in libraries, difficulties in functional screening, and time-intensive assay development. Process development is complicated by host system differences, scaling issues due to the small size increasing filtration and ultrafiltration losses, and the need for customized analytical methods. Nonetheless, VHHs represent a transformative platform in biologics. Their small size, stability, and design versatility make them ideal for next-generation therapeutics and diagnostics. As infrastructure and expertise grow, their potential is only limited by innovation. VHH antibodies are not just smallâ€”they are modular engineering platforms. The only limit is our imagination.

    [Original] Takeda, Iambic partner in latest pharma AI push
    Japanâ€™s largest pharmaceutical company, Takeda Pharmaceutical, has entered a multiyear collaboration with AI drug discovery firm Iambic Therapeutics, a deal potentially worth over $1.7 billion, to develop small molecule drugs for cancer and diseases of the digestive and immune systems. Takedaâ€™s research chief, Andy Plump, emphasized that â€œthe winners over the next five yearsâ€ will be those that fully integrate AI and automation into drug development, calling for a fundamental redesign of laboratories to enable this shift.     [Original] I asked AI to name my wife. To the hopelessly incorrect people it cited, my deepest apologies | Martin Rowson
    Satirist Martin Rowson has exposed the absurdity of artificial intelligence by asking Googleâ€™s AI to identify his wife, only to receive a series of increasingly bizarre and incorrect answers.     [Original] Businesses face extinction unless they protect nature, major report warns
    ShareSaveHelen Briggs,Environment correspondentandGwyndaf Hughes,Science videographerShareSaveWWTExperts are calling for urgent action to restore the natural systems that keep the economy runningBusinesses risk extinction themselves unless they protect and restore the natural world, scientists across the globe are warning. A major new report sets out how companies can shift from harmful approaches to ones that help restore nature. It comes amid major concerns over UK nature loss. The assessment, by Ipbes (Intergovernmental Science-Policy Platform on Biodiversity and Ecosystem Services), is based on contributions from leading scientists and approved by 150 governments. Businesses can either lead the way or "ultimately risk extinction... both of species in nature, but potentially also their own", said co-author Matt Jones, from the UN World Conservation Monitoring Centre in Cambridge. Ipbes found that all businesses, even those seemingly far-removed from it, rely on the services nature provides for free, from clean water to fertile soils. Co-chair, Prof Stephen Polasky, said the loss of biodiversity is among the most serious threats to business, "yet the twisted reality is that it often seems more profitable to businesses to degrade biodiversity than to protect it". Commenting on the report, Leigh Morris, International Director of the consortium of UK wildlife charities, The Wildlife Trusts, said we need "clear metrics and toolkits so businesses can get their own houses in order on biodiversity". For many UK businesses, engaging with nature protection has gone from "a nice-to-do" to a "must-do", he added. One example of how companies are working hand-in-hand with nature is at Steart Marshes in Somerset. Farmers and conservationists are managing land in ways that support both wildlife and agriculture. Cattle are grazed across the marshes to create healthy habitats for birds, insects and plants. Local farmer, Andy Darch, said the animals are helping in conservation. "They are eating different types of grasses and trampling areas that are important for wildlife," he said. "And because they are eating such a variety of plants, it produces a really high-quality beef at the end of the day." Steart Marshes also demonstrates how restoring nature can benefit local communities. Newly engineered flood banks protect nearby villages from rising waters, while the wetlands help absorb carbon and reduce pollution. Alys Laver, from the Wildfowl and Wetlands Trust, which runs the nature reserve, said farming and conservation are working hand-in-hand. "Not only are those flood banks an engineering marvel, they're providing flood protection for the local villages," she says. "On the back of that we're getting a product the farmers can utilise. So it's not a loss of farming it's just a change." The report pointed to everyday incentives that are driving nature's decline: It said better stewardship of nature is not a distant environmental issue but a core challenge for every boardroom. Yet, less than 1% of publicly reporting companies mention their impacts on biodiversity in their reports.

    [Original] Make-up brand Barry M bought by rival Warpaint
    ShareSaveArchie MitchellBusiness reporterShareSaveBBCDean Mero has run Barry M since the death of his father, Barry Mero, in 2014One of Britain's last family-run make-up brands has been bought out of administration by cosmetics rival, Warpaint. Barry M, which was set up in north London in 1982 by Barry Mero, collapsed earlier this month. Inspired by the punks and New Romantics of that era, analysts said Barry M had struggled to continue innovating and been overtaken by competitors. The Â£1.4m takeover by Warpaint will see the closure of Barry M's factory in the capital and puts 100 jobs at risk. Barry M had been a favourite of make-up fans and drag queens for its eye-catching colours. It is stocked in around 1,300 shops across the UK, including Superdrug, Boots, Sainsbury's and Tesco. Patrick O'Brien, retail research director at analytics firm GlobalData, said Barry M had failed to innovate and had instead been "more reactive". He told the BBC the company had also struggled as, despite being stocked in well-known retailers, it faced increasing competition from other brands at similar prices. O'Brien said Barry M had become "a small brand in a sea of new and fun names, which are generating traction through social media marketing". Since Mero's death in 2014, the company has been run by his son, Dean Mero. Speaking to the BBC in 2022, Dean said his father had been hoping to target the punks and New Romantics of the early 1980s. His father reasoned that these people were looking for "the blacks and the blues and the greens and the yellows", but why not offer more than that? He remembers his father saying that no other make-up company had produced 100 colours and Barry M would become the first to reach that goal. In the year to 28 February 2025, the most recent for which figures are available, Barry M reported sales of Â£15m. Alongside the deal, Warpaint also provided a trading update in which it said full-year profits would be lower due to a "challenging consumer and customer environment" as well as US tariffs. It said the levies, announced by US President Donald Trump, resulted in a Â£2m hit to its business as "uncertainty earlier in the year" led to "stalled momentum in the US". While sales for 2025 are expected to be higher at Â£105m, compared to Â£102m in the previous year, underlying profit is forecast to fall from Â£25m to Â£22m. Warpaint said taking over Barry M would increase its sales by expanding its reach in stores. The company owns a number of cosmetic and grooming lines including W7, Technic and Man'stuff. The Barry M deal, which is subject to court approval, follows Warpaint's acquisition of other brands last year, including Fish Soho and Dirty Works.

    [Original] The tech firms embracing a 72-hour working week
    Rilla, a New York-based AI tech company, promotes a high-intensity work culture through its recruitment website, touting perks like free meals, gym access, and health careâ€”while prominently warning job seekers: â€œPlease donâ€™t join if youâ€™re not excited aboutâ€¦ working ~70 hrs/week in person with some of the most ambitious people in NYC.â€ The company, which develops AI tools for monitoring sales reps, exemplifies the 996 work modelâ€”9 a.m. to 9 p.m., six days a weekâ€”popularized in China and now gaining traction in U.S. tech startups. Will Gao, Rillaâ€™s head of growth, defends the culture, describing employees as â€œOlympian athletesâ€ driven by passion and ambition, with flexible schedules that allow for late-night work and late arrivals. This mindset is fueled by the rapid pace of AI development, where venture-backed startups race to monetize innovations, creating pressure to outwork competitors. While 996 originated in China, championed by figures like Jack Ma and Richard Liu, it faced backlash over labor law violations and burnout, leading to a 2021 crackdown. Despite this, the culture persists, with critics like Baiduâ€™s Qu Jing facing public outrage for dismissing employee wellbeing. In the U.S., the trend is driven by AI startups like Browser-Use, co-founded by German entrepreneur Magnus MÃ¼ller, who lives in a â€œhacker-houseâ€ and views long hours as essential to breakthrough innovation. MÃ¼ller says he seeks employees â€œaddictedâ€ to their work, likening it to gaming. However, not all experts agree. Deedy Das of Menlo Ventures argues that equating long hours with productivity is a fallacy, warning that such cultures alienate experienced workers and cause burnout. He notes founders may work 70â€“80 hours, but that doesnâ€™t justify imposing the same on employees. Academic Tamara Myles highlights the power dynamics at play, noting that some workers comply due to economic pressure or visa dependence, not genuine enthusiasm. Health risks are well-documented: the WHO and ILO found that working over 55 hours weekly increases stroke risk by 35% and heart disease risk by 17%, contributing to 745,000 deaths globally in 2016. Productivity peaks around 40 hours, declining beyond that due to exhaustion. While some embrace 996 as a badge of honor, critics stress its unsustainability and long-term human cost.

    [Original] The shadowy world of abandoned oil tankers
    The number of abandoned oil tankers and commercial ships has surged to 410 in 2025, up nearly a third from 2024, affecting 6,223 merchant seamenâ€”up from 20 in 2016. The International Transport Workersâ€™ Federation (ITF) reports that 82% of abandoned vessels in 2025 were flagged under flags of convenience (FOCs), with 337 of the 410 ships falling into this category. These vessels, often aged, unseaworthy, uninsured, and operated by obscure owners, frequently sail under FOCs like Panama, Liberia, and the Marshall Islands, which collectively represent 46.5% of global merchant shipping by weight. The Gambia, previously uninvolved, hosted 35 oil tankers by March 2024, earning registration fees despite lacking oversight. Many of these ships are part of so-called â€œshadow fleets,â€ used to circumvent Western sanctions on oil exports from Russia, Iran, and Venezuela. Russia, for example, has continued exporting crude to China and India despite price caps, with some buyers now curbing purchases due to U.S. trade agreements. Ivan, a Russian senior deck officer, described life aboard an abandoned tanker carrying 750,000 barrels of Russian crudeâ€”valued at $50 millionâ€”sailing from Russiaâ€™s Far East to China. Abandoned in December, the crew had not been paid for months, leading to severe food shortages, deteriorating health, and unrest. The ITF intervened, securing payment up to December and delivering food and water. While some crew have been repatriated, most, including Ivan, remain on board. The ITF has recovered $16.5 million of the $25.8 million in unpaid wages globally in 2025. Indian sailors were most affected, with 1,125 cases (18%), followed by Filipinos (539) and Syrians (309). India responded by blacklisting 86 foreign vessels over abandonment and rights violations. Mark Dickinson of Nautilus International criticized FOC states for â€œa complete derogation of responsibility,â€ calling for stronger links between shipowners and flag states, a requirement already in international law but lacking universal definition. Ivanâ€™s vessel was flying a false Gambian flag; The Gambia later opened an inquiry, and the ship is now provisionally under another African nationâ€™s flag. ITF inspector Nathan Smith expects resolution only after a ship-to-ship transfer of oil in open sea. Ivan now vows to research vessel safety and sanctions status before joining future voyages. The growing reliance on shadow fleets for Russian oil exports underscores the urgent need for international cooperation to protect seafarers.

    [Original] Apprenticeship clearing system to be introduced
    ShareSaveAlicia CurryShareSaveGetty ImagesA new clearing-style system will be introduced to match young people who miss out on an apprenticeship with alternative placements, the government has said. Similar to university and college clearing - a process which matches students with institutions that have unfilled places - the online platform will provide information about available roles in their chosen area of interest. Ministers hope the pilot scheme will make apprenticeships easier to navigate and more appealing to young people weighing up their options. Prime Minister Keir Starmer said "outdated assumptions about how to make it into a successful career" have held young people back. He added: "We're unlocking opportunities for young people across the country by making it easier and faster to get the skills that matter, so more young people can build a secure life for themselves." Work and Pensions Secretary Pat McFadden said the scheme - being tested out this year - would "give those who miss out on their top-choice apprenticeship a second chance by matching them with another opportunity in their area". The new system, to be run in partnership with employers and mayoral strategic authorities, will also inform young people about potential earnings in the roles and long-term career prospects. It is part of government reforms aimed at delivering 50,000 more apprenticeships for young people, backed by Â£725m of funding. Ministers said the measures will play an integral role towards the government's ambition to get two-thirds of young people into higher-level learning or apprenticeships. A number of new placements will be announced by companies across the UK in National Apprenticeship Week, which starts on Monday. Among them is energy firm Centrica which has said it will create 500 new apprenticeships in 2026 as part of a two-year programme.

    [Original] Hollywood Braces for New Round of Labor Talks
    Just 26 months after the historic 2023 Hollywood strikes ended, negotiations for new contracts are set to begin on Monday, with SAG-AFTRA and the Alliance of Motion Picture and Television Producers preparing to discuss terms ahead of the May 1 expiration for writers and June 30 deadline for actors. The industry has since transformed, marked by slowed production, shrinking work opportunities for creatives, and the growing influence of generative artificial intelligence. SAG-AFTRA chief negotiator Duncan Crabtree-Ireland emphasized the unionâ€™s commitment to securing fair deals, stating, â€œWeâ€™re doing everything under our power to keep our members working,â€ while rejecting any agreement deemed unfair. The studio alliance expressed optimism, pledging a â€œfair deal that reflects our shared commitment to supporting our industryâ€™s talented performers and promoting long-term stability.â€ The Writers Guild of America will begin talks in March, followed by the Directors Guild of America, which did not strike in 2023. The 2023 dual strikesâ€”Hollywoodâ€™s first since the early 1960sâ€”halted production for months and caused significant economic disruption. Key issues then included compensation, working conditions, and AI use, with the latter expected to be a major focus again. Crabtree-Ireland said the union will push for stronger guardrails on AI. Sean Astin, newly elected SAG-AFTRA president, highlighted streaming residuals and other core concerns, noting that â€œour membersâ€™ lived experience is no longer properly reflected in the contract.â€ The Writers Guild has not yet detailed its top priorities, but replenishing health care reserves remains a central concern. Board member Marguerite MacIntyre said the issue of funding health care would be â€œa major element,â€ while Michele Mulroney, president of the western branch, called it â€œa headline issue.â€ Studios are expected to propose five-year contractsâ€”two years longer than the typical three-year dealsâ€”citing stability models from the NFL (10-year) and longshoremenâ€™s union (six-year). Union leaders argue that shorter contracts provide necessary flexibility amid rapid technological change. Christopher Nolan, newly elected DGA president, dismissed five-year extensions as â€œnot in any way a realistic proposal.â€ Greg Hessinger, the studio allianceâ€™s new head negotiator, is known to Crabtree-Ireland from past collaborations. The negotiator said Hessingerâ€™s appointment could signal a â€œlikely vibe shift,â€ expressing cautious optimism about improved industry relations. John Koblin covers the television industry for The Times.

    [Original] From Fishing Nets to Furniture: Turning Ocean Plastic Into Usable Products
    A brother-and-sister team in Spain, Julen and Amaia RodrÃ­guez SolÃ¡, founded Gravity Wave in 2019 to combat ocean pollution by recycling abandoned fishing netsâ€”known as â€œghost netsâ€â€”into sustainable products. These durable nylon nets, which can persist for centuries, entangle marine life and damage coral reefs. In September 2024, a five-day mission off the coast of SalobreÃ±a, a protected EU conservation zone, saw divers recover nearly 5,000 kilograms of nettingâ€”equivalent to the weight of an African elephantâ€”using specialized teams and cranes to lift the debris from 30 meters below the surface. The operation, led by JosÃ© Maria Fernandez and supported by Coral Soul, a marine restoration group, highlighted the scale of underwater pollution. Gravity Wave now collaborates with over 7,000 fishermen across 150 ports in Spain, Italy, and Greece to collect discarded nets and other ocean plastics. The company operates a full-cycle model, managing collection, recycling, and product development, using blockchain technology to verify environmental impact. Its recycled materials are transformed into plastic pellets, panels, and custom designs for furniture, stadium seating, and decorative elements. In Valenciaâ€™s industrial zone, former ghost nets are processed into shiny turquoise pellets and panels, used by architects, hotels, and industry partners. To date, Gravity Wave has collected 1,400 tons of plastic and fishing nets, with over 700 tons processed. Despite challengesâ€”including European waste transport regulations that necessitated local recycling partnerships in Italy and Greece, and initial reluctance from recyclers due to machinery risksâ€”the company has proven that ocean plastic can be repurposed profitably. â€œWe are showing that plastic can have a second life, and that businesses can profit while protecting the environment,â€ said Amaia RodrÃ­guez SolÃ¡. The initiative not only cleans the oceans but also creates economic value, supporting waste collectors, recyclers, and manufacturers.

    [Original] Why the N.F.L. Booked Bad Bunny for the Super Bowl Halftime Show
    Bad Bunnyâ€™s controversial stance on U.S. immigration policy has placed the N.F.L. in a delicate position, yet the league chose the Latin superstar to headline the 2024 Super Bowl halftime showâ€”a decision rooted in a strategic shift begun in 2018. That year, the league faced intense backlash over players kneeling during the national anthem to protest police brutality, a movement initiated by Colin Kaepernick in 2016. President Trump publicly criticized the league and urged team owners to fire players who refused to stand, creating a firestorm involving fans, sponsors, and politicians. In response, some artists declined to perform at the Super Bowl, leading to widespread criticism of the 2019 halftime show featuring Maroon 5. To repair its image and reconnect with younger, more diverse audiences, the N.F.L. pivoted. Robert K. Kraft, owner of the New England Patriots and a key figure in music and Hollywood, advocated for the league to align with social justice initiatives. He and Commissioner Roger Goodell met secretly with Jay-Z in Los Angeles. In August 2019, the league partnered with Jay-Zâ€™s Roc Nation to produce the halftime show and support social justice efforts. The alliance gave the N.F.L. credibility, access to top-tier artists, and a platform to reach broader demographics. Since then, the halftime show has featured a diverse roster of stars, including Jennifer Lopez, Shakira (with a cameo by Bad Bunny), Dr. Dre, Snoop Dogg, Eminem, Mary J. Blige, Rihanna, and Kendrick Lamar. While the N.F.L. approves the final performers, Roc Nation selects the acts. Bad Bunnyâ€™s inclusion was a natural choice from a musical standpoint: he has broken global ticketing records, achieved 15 Top 10 hits, and won Album of the Year at the Grammys in 2023. Though many N.F.L. owners and executives may not be familiar with Bad Bunnyâ€™s music or his vocal opposition to the Trump administrationâ€™s immigration crackdown, they recognize the necessity of accommodating such views to attract top talent and their fan bases. â€œI donâ€™t want to pick the music that I listen to â€™cause none of you would come to the halftime show,â€ Goodell said in October. He credited Jay-Z with balancing artistic integrity and fan appeal, noting that Jay-Z understands both the music industry and the leagueâ€™s interests without pushing ideological boundaries. Ken Belson, a New York Times reporter covering sports, power, and money in professional leagues, reported on the developments.

    [Original] Can AI Chatbots Write Emotionally Rich Romance Books?
    Coral Hart, a veteran romance novelist published by Harlequin and Mills & Boon, launched an eight-month experiment using artificial intelligence to write romance novels under 21 pen names. She produced over 200 books in diverse subgenresâ€”ranging from dark mafia romances to sweet teen storiesâ€”self-published on Amazon, selling approximately 50,000 copies and earning six figures. Using AI, she generated full novels in under an hour, including one about a rancher and a city girl, completed in 45 minutes. While AI tools like Grok and NovelAI produced explicit scenes, they lacked emotional depth and often felt mechanical. Claude by Anthropic delivered elegant prose but struggled with romantic banter and sexual tension, frequently defaulting to clichÃ©d tropes like â€œtangled in the sheets.â€ Hart developed workarounds, such as feeding specific kinks and emphasizing narrative necessity to bypass restrictions. She now teaches AI-assisted writing through her business, Plot Prose, having trained over 1,600 writers, and is launching a proprietary AI tool priced between $80 and $250 monthly. Despite her success, Hart maintains anonymity for her AI-assisted pen names due to stigma, though she plans to launch three openly AI-generated ones. Romance, the best-selling genre accounting for over 20% of adult fiction print sales, is particularly vulnerable to AI disruption due to its reliance on predictable tropes like â€œenemies-to-loversâ€ and guaranteed â€œH.E.A.â€ (happily ever after). However, AI remains controversial: readers and authors alike express concern over authenticity, with some calling AI-generated works â€œtheft machines.â€ Social media backlash erupted when AI prompts were accidentally left in published novels. While Amazon requires disclosure of AI use on its platform, it does not mandate public disclaimers. Experts like Christa DÃ©sir of Bloom Books warn AI detection will soon become ineffective. Hart cautions that AI-generated sex scenes often suffer from awkward phrasingâ€”such as â€œhis turgid manhoodâ€â€”and overuse of clichÃ©s, urging writers to create â€œick listsâ€ and suggest creative settings like winery tanks or rooftop greenhouses. Even AI advocates like psychologist Sonia Rompoti, who wrote 10 novels in a year using Sudowrite, admit AI fails to capture human intimacy, often exaggerating physical traits like weight in erotic scenes. Despite efficiency gains, many readers and writers, including ZoÃ« Mahler of The Ripped Bodice, reject AI romance, arguing it lacks the emotional authenticity central to the genre. â€œRomance is about human connection,â€ she said. â€œWhy read a story written by a machine trying to emulate that?â€

    [Original] Maxwell won't answer questions from Congress, lawyer says
    Ghislaine Maxwell, serving a 20-year sentence for sex trafficking related to her role in Jeffrey Epsteinâ€™s abuse network, plans to invoke her Fifth Amendment right to remain silent during a closed-door virtual deposition before the U.S. House Oversight Committee on Monday, her lawyer David Oscar Markus confirmed. Maxwell, incarcerated at a Texas prison, will instead read a prepared statement, according to Democratic Representative Ro Khanna, who chairs the committeeâ€™s subcommittee on oversight. Maxwell was convicted in 2021 for recruiting underage girls for Epstein, who died in prison in 2019. She is currently seeking a pardon from former President Donald Trump and has been accused of lying to federal officials. Khanna intends to question Maxwell about a 2023 court filing in which she named four co-conspirators and 25 others not indicted in the Epstein investigation. He also plans to ask about her and Epsteinâ€™s alleged social ties to Trump, including whether Trump ever discussed a potential pardon with her legal team. Trump has consistently denied any wrongdoing, stating he severed ties with Epstein decades ago and has not been accused of crimes by Epsteinâ€™s victims. Khanna noted that Maxwellâ€™s decision to invoke the Fifth Amendment appears inconsistent with her prior conduct, as she did not do so during a July meeting with Deputy Attorney General Todd Blancheâ€”formerly Trumpâ€™s personal attorneyâ€”when discussing similar topics. In that meeting, Maxwell told Blanche she did not witness inappropriate conduct by Trump or former President Bill Clinton and denied the existence of a rumored Epstein â€œclient list.â€ The deposition, originally scheduled for August 2023, was postponed at Maxwellâ€™s lawyersâ€™ request to await a Supreme Court ruling on her case. Starting Monday, members of Congress may view unredacted versions in person at the DOJ. Epstein survivors released a video Sunday urging greater transparency, particularly regarding redactions and withheld files. Blanche has denied any cover-up, stating the DOJ has not withheld information about individuals it knows about or chosen not to prosecute.

    [Original] Seahawks dominate Patriots to win Super Bowl
    The Seattle Seahawks defeated the New England Patriots 29-13 in Super Bowl 60 at Leviâ€™s Stadium, claiming their second championship with a dominant defensive performance dubbed â€œthe Dark Side.â€ The game, contested by two of the NFLâ€™s top defenses, saw Seattle record six sacks, force three turnovers, and score a defensive touchdown. Briton Aden Durde, the 46-year-old defensive co-ordinator, became the first overseas coach to win the Super Bowl, leading a unit that has become synonymous with elite pressure and discipline. Quarterback Drake Maye, the NFLâ€™s second-year signal-caller and runner-up for MVP, was stifled, completing just 52 yards and failing to register a first down in the first half. His struggles culminated in two interceptions, one returned 45 yards for a touchdown by linebacker Uchenna Nwosu. Tight end AJ Barner scored the gameâ€™s first touchdown early in the fourth quarter following Mayeâ€™s first turnover. Jason Meyers kicked a record five field goals, while defensive end Derick Hall forced a fumble recovered by Byron Murphy, who also recorded two sacks. Devon Witherspoon, a cornerback, added a sack, highlighting the depth of Seattleâ€™s pass rush despite limited season totals. The Patriots, playing in their first Super Bowl since 2019 following the departures of Tom Brady and Bill Belichick, were unable to establish a running game or get star receiver Stefon Diggs involved. Maye briefly sparked hope with a touchdown pass to Mack Hollins, cutting the deficit to 19-7, but was intercepted on the next two possessions.     [Original] Outrage as South Korean official suggests 'importing' foreign women to boost birth rate
    ShareSaveKoh EweShareSaveBloomberg via Getty ImagesSouth Korea has the lowest birth rate in the worldA South Korean official who suggested the country "import young women" from "Vietnam or Sri Lanka" to boost its birth-rate has been expelled from his party. Kim Hee-soo, the head of the southern Jindo County, said the woman could be married off to "young men in rural areas" during a town hall last week. The suggestion comes as South Korea continues to grapple with the lowest birth-rates in the world, which could see the country's 50 million-strong population drop by half in 60 years. But Kim's statement, which was televised, did not go down well - triggering a diplomatic protest from Vietnam, days of public anger and his expulsion from the ruling Democratic Party. Attempts by Kim to defuse the outrage with an apology a day after the town hall appear to have failed. The town hall had been called to discuss a potential merger between the province where Jindo County is located and a nearby city - something regions with shrinking populations are looking at for administrative reasons. Kim said his comment had been intended to highlight population issues in rural regions but admitted the language he had used was "inappropriate", local media reported. South Jeolla Province also issued a formal apology for Kim's "inappropriate remarks", which it said "has caused deep pain to Vietnamese people and to women", local media reported. The Vietnamese Embassy in Seoul had condemned Kim's remarks, saying in a statement on Facebook that his words were "not simply a matter of expression but a matter of values and attitudes towards migrant women and minority groups". Sri Lanka authorities have not publicly addressed the controversy. The Democratic Party's Supreme Council had voted unanimously to expel Kim, a party spokesperson told reporters on Monday. Meanwhile, activists for women and migrant rights are reportedly planning to hold a rally in front of Jindo County Office on Tuesday over Kim's comments.

    [Original] Christchurch shooter seeks to overturn guilty plea
